Every\n\t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\n\t// processing set.\n\tqueue Queue[t]\n\n\t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\n\tdirty set[t]\n\n\t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\n\t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. When we finish\n\t// processing something and remove it from this set, we'll check if\n\t// it's in the dirty set, and if so, add it to the queue.\n\tprocessing set[t]\n\n\tcond *sync.Cond\n\n\tshuttingDown bool\n\tdrain        bool\n\n\tmetrics queueMetrics[t]\n\n\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod time.Duration\n\tclock                      clock.WithTicker\n}\n\ntype empty struct{}\ntype set[t comparable] map[t]empty\n\nfunc (s set[t]) has(item t) bool {\n\t_, exists := s[item]\n\treturn exists\n}\n\nfunc (s set[t]) insert(item t) {\n\ts[item] = empty{}\n}\n\nfunc (s set[t]) delete(item t) {\n\tdelete(s, item)\n}\n\nfunc (s set[t]) len() int {\n\treturn len(s)\n}\n\n// Add marks item as needing processing.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Add(item T) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tif q.shuttingDown {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tif q.dirty.has(item) {\n\t\t// the same item is added again before it is processed, call the Touch\n\t\t// function if the queue cares about it (for e.g, reset its priority)\n\t\tif !q.processing.has(item) {\n\t\t\tq.queue.Touch(item)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.metrics.add(item)\n\n\tq.dirty.insert(item)\n\tif q.processing.has(item) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.queue.Push(item)\n\tq.cond.Signal()\n}\n\n// Len returns the current queue length, for informational purposes only. You\n// shouldn't e.g. gate a call to Add() or Get() on Len() being a particular\n// value, that can't be synchronized properly.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Len() int {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\treturn q.queue.Len()\n}\n\n// Get blocks until it can return an item to be processed. If shutdown = true,\n// the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\n// have finished processing it.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\n\t\tq.cond.Wait()\n\t}\n\tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\n\t\t// We must be shutting down.\n\t\treturn *new(T), true\n\t}\n\n\titem = q.queue.Pop()\n\n\tq.metrics.get(item)\n\n\tq.processing.insert(item)\n\tq.dirty.delete(item)\n\n\treturn item, false\n}\n\n// Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\n// while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\n// re-processing.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.metrics.done(item)\n\n\tq.processing.delete(item)\n\tif q.dirty.has(item) {\n\t\tq.queue.Push(item)\n\t\tq.cond.Signal()\n\t} else if q.processing.len() == 0 {\n\t\tq.cond.Signal()\n\t}\n}\n\n// ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it and\n// immediately instruct the worker goroutines to exit.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.drain = false\n\tq.shuttingDown = true\n\tq.cond.Broadcast()\n}\n\n// ShutDownWithDrain will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. As soon\n// as the worker goroutines have \"drained\", i.e: finished processing and called\n// Done on all existing items in the queue; they will be instructed to exit and\n// ShutDownWithDrain will return. Hence: a strict requirement for using this is;\n// your workers must ensure that Done is called on all items in the queue once\n// the shut down has been initiated, if that is not the case: this will block\n// indefinitely. It is, however, safe to call ShutDown after having called\n// ShutDownWithDrain, as to force the queue shut down to terminate immediately\n// without waiting for the drainage.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShutDownWithDrain() {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.drain = true\n\tq.shuttingDown = true\n\tq.cond.Broadcast()\n\n\tfor q.processing.len() != 0 && q.drain {\n\t\tq.cond.Wait()\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShuttingDown() bool {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\treturn q.shuttingDown\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWorkLoop() {\n\tt := q.clock.NewTicker(q.unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod)\n\tdefer t.Stop()\n\tfor range t.C() {\n\t\tif !func() bool {\n\t\t\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\t\t\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\t\t\tif !q.shuttingDown {\n\t\t\t\tq.metrics.updateUnfinishedWork()\n\t\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn false\n\n\t\t}() {\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n","numLines":370,"startLine":1,"totalLines":370}}}

working queue\n\tkey, quit := c.queue.Get()\n\tif quit {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\t// Tell the queue that we are done with processing this key. This unblocks the key for other workers\n\t// This allows safe parallel processing because two pods with the same key are never processed in\n\t// parallel.\n\tdefer c.queue.Done(key)\n\n\t// Invoke the method containing the business logic\n\terr := c.syncToStdout(key)\n\t// Handle the error if something went wrong during the execution of the business logic\n\tc.handleErr(err, key)\n\treturn true\n}\n\n// syncToStdout is the business logic of the controller. In this controller it simply prints\n// information about the pod to stdout. In case an error happened, it has to simply return the error.\n// The retry logic should not be part of the business logic.\nfunc (c *Controller) syncToStdout(key string) error {\n\tobj, exists, err := c.indexer.GetByKey(key)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tklog.Errorf(\"Fetching object with key %s from store failed with %v\", key, err)\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tif !exists {\n\t\t// Below we will warm up our cache with a Pod, so that we will see a delete for one pod\n\t\tfmt.Printf(\"Pod %s does not exist anymore\\n\", key)\n\t} else {\n\t\t// Note that you also have to check the uid if you have a local controlled resource, which\n\t\t// is dependent on the actual instance, to detect that a Pod was recreated with the same name\n\t\tfmt.Printf(\"Sync/Add/Update for Pod %s\\n\", obj.(*v1.Pod).GetName())\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// handleErr checks if an error happened and makes sure we will retry later.\nfunc (c *Controller) handleErr(err error, key string) {\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\t// Forget about the #AddRateLimited history of the key on every successful synchronization.\n\t\t// This ensures that future processing of updates for this key is not delayed because of\n\t\t// an outdated error history.\n\t\tc.queue.Forget(key)\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// This controller retries 5 times if something goes wrong. After that, it stops trying.\n\tif c.queue.NumRequeues(key) < 5 {\n\t\tklog.Infof(\"Error syncing pod %v: %v\", key, err)\n\n\t\t// Re-enqueue the key rate limited. Based on the rate limiter on the\n\t\t// queue and the re-enqueue history, the key will be processed later again.\n\t\tc.queue.AddRateLimited(key)\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tc.queue.Forget(key)\n\t// Report to an external entity that, even after several retries, we could not successfully process this key\n\truntime.HandleError(err)\n\tklog.Infof(\"Dropping pod %q out of the queue: %v\", key, err)\n}\n\n// Run begins watching and syncing.\nfunc (c *Controller) Run(workers int, stopCh chan struct{}) {\n\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n\n\t// Let the workers stop when we are done\n\tdefer c.queue.ShutDown()\n\tklog.Info(\"Starting Pod controller\")\n\n\tgo c.informer.Run(stopCh)\n\n\t// Wait for all involved caches to be synced, before processing items from the queue is started\n\tif !cache.WaitForCacheSync(stopCh, c.informer.HasSynced) {\n\t\truntime.HandleError(fmt.Errorf(\"Timed out waiting for caches to sync\"))\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < workers; i++ {\n\t\tgo wait.Until(c.runWorker, time.Second, stopCh)\n\t}\n\n\t<-stopCh\n\tklog.Info(\"Stopping Pod controller\")\n}\n\nfunc (c *Controller) runWorker() {\n\tfor c.processNextItem() {\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc main() {\n\tvar kubeconfig string\n\tvar master string\n\n\tflag.StringVar(&kubeconfig, \"kubeconfig\", \"\", \"absolute path to the kubeconfig file\")\n\tflag.StringVar(&master, \"master\", \"\", \"master url\")\n\tflag.Parse()\n\n\t// creates the connection\n\tconfig, err := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(master, kubeconfig)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tklog.Fatal(err)\n\t}\n\n\t// creates the clientset\n\tclientset, err := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tklog.Fatal(err)\n\t}\n\n\t// create the pod watcher\n\tpodListWatcher := cache.NewListWatchFromClient(clientset.CoreV1().RESTClient(), \"pods\", v1.NamespaceDefault, fields.Everything())\n\n\t// create the workqueue\n\tqueue := workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue(workqueue.DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter[string]())\n\n\t// Bind the workqueue to a cache with the help of an informer. This way we make sure that\n\t// whenever the cache is updated, the pod key is added to the workqueue.\n\t// Note that when we finally process the item from the workqueue, we might see a newer version\n\t// of the Pod than the version which was responsible for triggering the update.\n\tindexer, informer := cache.NewIndexerInformer(podListWatcher, &v1.Pod{}, 0, cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n\t\tAddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n\t\t\tkey, err := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n\t\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\t\tqueue.Add(key)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t},\n\t\tUpdateFunc: func(old interface{}, new interface{}) {\n\t\t\tkey, err := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(new)\n\t\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\t\tqueue.Add(key)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t},\n\t\tDeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n\t\t\t// IndexerInformer uses a delta queue, therefore for deletes we have to use this\n\t\t\t// key function.\n\t\t\tkey, err := cache.DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n\t\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\t\tqueue.Add(key)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t},\n\t}, cache.Indexers{})\n\n\tcontroller := NewController(queue, indexer, informer)\n\n\t// We can now warm up the cache for initial synchronization.\n\t// Let's suppose that we knew about a pod \"mypod\" on our last run, therefore add it to the cache.\n\t// If this pod is not there anymore, the controller will be notified about the removal after the\n\t// cache has synchronized.\n\tindexer.Add(&v1.Pod{\n\t\tObjectMeta: meta_v1.ObjectMeta{\n\t\t\tName:      \"mypod\",\n\t\t\tNamespace: v1.NamespaceDefault,\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\n\t// Now let's start the controller\n\tstop := make(chan struct{})\n\tdefer close(stop)\n\tgo controller.Run(1, stop)\n\n\t// Wait forever\n\tselect {}\n}\n","numLines":221,"startLine":1,"totalLines":221}}}

TypedInterface specifies the contract with methods for adding items, getting the next item to process, and marking items as done.\\n\\n2. **Rate Limiting Queue (rate_limiting_queue.go)**: TypedRateLimitingInterface extends TypedDelayingInterface with rate-limited re-enqueueing capabilities through AddRateLimited, Forget, and NumRequeues methods. RateLimitingInterface is the deprecated non-generic variant.\\n\\n3. **Rate Limiters (default_rate_limiters.go)**: Two main implementations are provided:\\n   - **ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter** (TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter): Implements exponential backoff with baseDelay*2^(num-failures) logic, configurable with maximum delay constraints. The core implementation resides in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/.\\n\\n## Core Components\\n\\n### Queue Interfaces and Implementations\\n\\n1. **Basic Queue (queue.go)**: The TypedInterface interface and Typed struct define the fundamental queue operations with methods Add(item T), Get() (item T, shutdown bool), Done(item T), Len(), ShutDown(), ShutDownWithDrain(), and ShuttingDown(). The implementation uses internal dirty and processing sets to track item states, ensuring items are processed exactly once and can be re-added if marked dirty during processing.\\n\\n2. **Delaying Queue (delaying_queue.go)**: The TypedDelayingInterface extends TypedInterface with the AddAfter(item T, duration time.Duration) method, enabling delayed re-enqueueing. The internal Typed struct manages a heap-based waitingFor queue to delay items until ready.\\n\\n3. **Rate Limiting Queue (rate_limiting_queue.go)**: The TypedRateLimitingInterface extends TypedDelayingInterface with rate-limited re-enqueueing: AddRateLimited(item T), Forget(item T), and NumRequeues(item T) int. The internal rateLimitingType struct wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and TypedRateLimiter. RateLimitingInterface is the deprecated non-generic type alias.\\n\\n### Rate Limiters (default_rate_limiters.go)\\n\\n1. **TypedRateLimiter[T comparable]**: Core interface with methods When(item T) time.Duration, Forget(item T), and NumRequeues(item T) int. RateLimiter is the deprecated non-generic alias.\\n\\n2. **ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter / TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter[T]**: Implements exponential backoff with the formula baseDelay * 2^(num-failures), capped at maxDelay. The When() method computes backoff using fast-path overflow checking. NumRequeues() returns the failure count for an item. Forget() clears the failure count when an item succeeds. Created with NewItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(baseDelay, maxDelay) or NewTypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter[T](baseDelay, maxDelay).\\n\\n3. **BucketRateLimiter / TypedBucketRateLimiter[T]**: Adapts golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter (token bucket algorithm) to the workqueue API. The When() method reserves a token and returns the delay. NumRequeues() always returns 0 (no per-item tracking). Forget() is a no-op. Provides global rate limiting across all items.\\n\\n4. **DefaultControllerRateLimiter / DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter[T]()**: Factory function creating a TypedMaxOfRateLimiter that combines ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter (5ms base, 1000s max) and BucketRateLimiter (10 qps, 100 bucket). Returns the maximum delay from both limiters, providing both per-item exponential backoff and overall rate limiting.\\n\\n5. **TypedMaxOfRateLimiter[T]**: Combines multiple TypedRateLimiter instances, returning the maximum When() delay and maximum NumRequeues() value. Calls Forget() on all constituent limiters.\\n\\n## Controller Reconcile Loop Pattern\\n\\nControllers implement the standard reconcile loop using three core queue operations:\\n\\n### Example: staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/workqueue/main.go\\nThe canonical example demonstrates the complete pattern in Controller.processNextItem():\\n- queue.Get() blocks until work is available, returning a key and shutdown flag\\n- Deferred queue.Done(key) marks work completion\\n- Calls sync function (syncToStdout) with business logic\\n- Controller.handleErr() implements retry logic: queue.Forget(key) on success or after NumRequeues() >= 5, otherwise queue.AddRateLimited(key) to requeue with rate limiting\\n- Controller.Run() spawns worker goroutines calling runWorker() which loops on processNextItem()\\n\\n### Production Controllers\\n\\n1. **pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go**: DeploymentController uses TypedRateLimitingInterface[string] queue field. The processNextWorkItem() method (lines 487-498) implements the core pattern: queue.Get() retrieves the next deployment key, deferred queue.Done(key) ensures cleanup, syncHandler() processes the deployment. The handleErr() method (lines 500-520) calls queue.Forget(key) on success or if NumRequeues(key) >= maxRetries (15), otherwise queue.AddRateLimited(key) for exponential backoff retry with (5ms * 2^n) delays.\\n\\n2. **pkg/controller/bootstrap/tokencleaner.go**: TokenCleaner manages bootstrap token expiration. The processNextWorkItem() method (lines 145-160) follows the pattern: queue.Get() retrieves the next secret key, deferred queue.Done(key), syncFunc() checks and removes expired tokens. On error, queue.AddRateLimited() requeues; on success, queue.Forget() clears tracking.\\n\\n3. **pkg/controller/bootstrap/bootstrapsigner.go**: BootstrapSigner processes bootstrap CSR signing requests. Uses the queue in its syncLoop() with queue.Get() and queue.Done() pattern.\\n\\n## Design Benefits\\n\\nThe work queue design ensures:\\n- **Fair distribution**: FIFO ordering with per-worker processing\\n- **Reliability**: Deferred Done() ensures items aren't lost even if a worker crashes\\n- **Exponential backoff**: Failed items experience increasingly long delays (5ms, 10ms, 20ms, 40ms, ..., capped at 1000s)\\n- **Overall rate limiting**: Token bucket prevents overwhelming dependent systems (e.g., API server)\\n- **Idempotency support**: The same item can be processed multiple times safely, with the cache ensuring consistent state\\n- **Production-ready**: Suitable for managing thousands of objects in large Kubernetes clusters\"\n}\nEOF\ncat /workspace/answer.json\n","description":"Create comprehensive answer.json with all findings"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":679,"cache_read_input_tokens":57974,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":679},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dd47bb3e-d7eb-418e-a7c0-29ca38cdacae","uuid":"5a097280-a50d-4389-b1cf-cfaf409bb87e"}

The When() method computes backoff using fast-path overflow checking. NumRequeues() returns the failure count for an item. Forget() clears the failure count when an item succeeds. Created with NewItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(baseDelay, maxDelay) or NewTypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter[T](baseDelay, maxDelay).\\n\\n3. **BucketRateLimiter / TypedBucketRateLimiter[T]**: Adapts golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter (token bucket algorithm) to the workqueue API. Uses the queue in its syncLoop() with queue.Get() and queue.Done() pattern.\\n\\n## Design Benefits\\n\\nThe work queue design ensures:\\n- **Fair distribution**: FIFO ordering with per-worker processing\\n- **Reliability**: Deferred Done() ensures items aren't lost even if a worker crashes\\n- **Exponential backoff**: Failed items experience increasingly long delays (5ms, 10ms, 20ms, 40ms, ..., capped at 1000s)\\n- **Overall rate limiting**: Token bucket prevents overwhelming dependent systems (e.g., API server)\\n- **Idempotency support**: The same item can be processed multiple times safely, with the cache ensuring consistent state\\n- **Production-ready**: Suitable for managing thousands of objects in large Kubernetes clusters\"\n}","stderr":"","interrupted":false,"isImage":false,"noOutputExpected":false}}
